  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_aae60079-94d2-48e7-ae96-26855693f2e2'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer11691229823700121649">Lowen Ashleigh is a struggling writer on the brink of financial ruin when she accepts the job offer of a lifetime. Jeremy Crawford, husband of bestselling author Verity Crawford, has hired Lowen to complete the remaining books in a successful series his injured wife is unable to finish.<br/><br/>Lowen arrives at the Crawford home, ready to sort through years of Verity's notes and ou</span>
  <span id="freeText11691229823700121649" style="display:none">Lowen Ashleigh is a struggling writer on the brink of financial ruin when she accepts the job offer of a lifetime. Jeremy Crawford, husband of bestselling author Verity Crawford, has hired Lowen to complete the remaining books in a successful series his injured wife is unable to finish.<br /><br />Lowen arrives at the Crawford home, ready to sort through years of Verity's notes and outlines, hoping to find enough material to get her started. What Lowen doesn't expect to uncover in the chaotic office is an unfinished autobiography Verity never intended for anyone to read. Page after page of bone-chilling admissions, including Verity's recollection of what really happened the day her daughter died.<br /><br />Lowen decides to keep the manuscript hidden from Jeremy, knowing its contents would devastate the already grieving father. But as Lowen's feelings for Jeremy begin to intensify, she recognizes all the ways she could benefit if he were to read his wife's words. After all, no matter how devoted Jeremy is to his injured wife, a truth this horrifying would make it impossible for him to continue to love her.<br /><br />A standalone romantic thriller from #1 New York Times bestselling author Colleen Hoover.</span>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/20758488-brittany"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1369766933i/20758488._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/20758488-brittany">Brittany</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I think the manuscript Verity was the true Verity and the letter was her trying to cover her tracks. She said in the letter that she wrote it the nigh<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I think the manuscript Verity was the true Verity and the letter was her trying to cover her tracks. She said in the letter that she wrote it the night Lowen and Jeremy were having sex. Earlier that day was when Lowen revealed to Verity that she read the manuscript. I don't have the book to reference exactly what she said, but it was something about how she hoped she died choking the same way she tried to do that to her infant daughter. I think that was the moment she panicked and wrote the letter that night.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2620503226" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2620503226" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2620503226?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=2018-releases">2018-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult-thriller-mystery">adult-thriller-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult-romance">adult-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2620503226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10226255771513524517"><strong>Me, rollerblading into my therapist’s office with sunglasses and a piña colada and dropping this book on the desk with a resounding thud:</strong>  Karen, we have much to talk about.<br/><br/>Why read <em>Verity</em> when you can just pull out a Ouija board and summon a demon? I'm sure it’ll have the same effect. I finished this book feeling completely sapped of life, as if I've been bleeding freely for the past few hours instead of simply reading. I wish I could just shake my head to dissolve the memory of that ending, to</span>
  <span id="freeText10226255771513524517" style="display:none"><strong>Me, rollerblading into my therapist’s office with sunglasses and a piña colada and dropping this book on the desk with a resounding thud:</strong>  Karen, we have much to talk about.<br /><br />Why read <em>Verity</em> when you can just pull out a Ouija board and summon a demon? I'm sure it’ll have the same effect. I finished this book feeling completely sapped of life, as if I've been bleeding freely for the past few hours instead of simply reading. I wish I could just shake my head to dissolve the memory of that ending, to disarrange it somehow. My mind is still at war with itself, because, of all the things I’d braced myself for, <em>that</em> was not it.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <u>So, what’s this book about?</u>
  </strong>
</blockquote><br /><br />Lowen Ashleigh is set free from the long tedium of her daily life when she’s employed by Jeremy Crawford to ghostwrite the remaining books in a popular series his wife, Verity, is unable to finish due to an unfortunate accident. Lowe acquiesces in the spirit of hope: that this opportunity would help her acquire some small measure of celebrity that would be pure oxygen to the fire of her career. But nothing prepares Lowe for the purity of dread that clamps down her like a vise when she stumbles upon Verity’s autobiography. Verity’s secrets soon take up so much space in the house that there is barely any room left for Lowe’s body. Now she has to force what she’s reading into what she knew of Verity, Jeremy, and their lives together. She has to weave it in among what she expected.<br /><br />Sooner or later, the whole truth would spill, and this fraught waiting would come to an end—with havoc, and screaming, and loss.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“After all, this is a house full of Chronics. The next tragedy is already long overdue.”</em>
  <br />
  <br />
</blockquote>I relish books that make me backtrack my own declarations of preference, the ones that catch me completely off-guard, astonish me, keep me on my toes. <strong><em>Verity</em> is not at all what I expected, and I think it is all the better for it.</strong> I’d gone on in mystery, but not without speculation and a vast deal of skepticism. I made the mistake of perceiving this book through the haze of my opinions on Hoover’s early books, and it didn’t look quite like I remembered. I’ve never been happier to be so astronomically wrong, because this book absolutely lives up to the buzz.<br /><br /><em>Verity</em> is a fiendishly clever, mind-bending whirligig of a book. It’s a hall of mirrors where everything is a vacant reflection, including the people who live there. Hoover lures and tricks and sets obstacles to drive you into her toils. She wields her unreliable characters to stunning effect, confounding, disturbing and delighting in turn, and draws you into a world where illusion informs reality and time enfolds hauntingly. Not only is nothing what it seems, it’s not even what it seems after it’s been revealed to be not what it seems. I was entrapped in this story long before I even realized that the net has been cast.<br /><br /><strong>I love how wild the energy was in this book, barely controllable yet perfectly controlled</strong>. Hoover drapes Lowe’s unease and confusion over the reader by keeping us in the same disconcerting darkness. Danger pulses all around. Every page is very thin ice to skate on. You can scarcely see the freshly hideous future taking shape ahead of you, yet you can feel it all the same. I have a quirk of prudence in me that’s hard to break and if I were Lowe, I’d have gotten the <em>hell</em> out of that place. I couldn’t fathom how her fear couldn’t properly kindle. I’d have been impressed if I weren’t too distressed and I’d have appreciated her courage if I weren’t too preoccupied repeating a litany of “GET OUT OF THERE” in my head.<br /><br />And, <em>oh my God</em>, the ending. <strong>It struck me backhanded</strong>. <em>Verity</em> offers you no solidity of truth that you could hold in your hands. Even as I was reading the last chapter, I was mining it for clues, trying to make sense of something so innately senseless. Everything I’ve read up until that point felt like a false memory, and I was left shaking my fist at the whole book for leaving me on such a hideous note as it did.<br /><br />In conclusion, stories like <em>Verity</em>, are the reason I’m going to be one of those parents in their forties that make their kids go to sleep at 6 pm so they can drink scotch in the bath and have an existential crisis about that book they read back in 2018!<br /><br /><blockquote>✨ <a href="http://amzn.eu/9Jnbkf3" rel="nofollow noopener">wishlist</a> ✨ <a href="https://runawaywithdreamthieves.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ✨ <a href="https://twitter.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ✨ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ✨</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="10226255771513524517" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2618745623" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2618745623" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528750408p2/9684061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2618745623?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=best-of-the-best">best-of-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=dark-and-twisted">dark-and-twisted</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=mind-fuck">mind-fuck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=unputdownable">unputdownable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=creepy">creepy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=unforgettable-reads">unforgettable-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2618745623" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14370197171707202463"><i><b>Bold</b>. Unrelenting. All-consuming. Creepy. Unputdownable.</i><br/><br/>What I’ve come to appreciate most about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5430144.Colleen_Hoover' title='Colleen Hoover' rel='nofollow noopener'> Colleen Hoover</a>’s work—whether it’s an emotionally charged love story <u>or</u> in this case, her first go at suspense—is her penchant for pushing boundaries. For telling the <i>unexpected</i> story. <br/><br/><i>“It’s got bad things in it. Bad words, bad people, bad scenes.”</i><br/><br/>Hoover preempted <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11925514.Code_Name_Verity__Code_Name_Verity___1_' title='Code Name Verity (Code Name Verity, #1) by Elizabeth E. Wein' rel='nofollow noopener'> Verity</a>’s release with a warning of sorts—although facetious and comical in delivery, it’s something sensitive readers should take to hear</span>
  <span id="freeText14370197171707202463" style="display:none"><i><b>Bold</b>. Unrelenting. All-consuming. Creepy. Unputdownable.</i><br /><br />What I’ve come to appreciate most about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5430144.Colleen_Hoover" title="Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener"> Colleen Hoover</a>’s work—whether it’s an emotionally charged love story <u>or</u> in this case, her first go at suspense—is her penchant for pushing boundaries. For telling the <i>unexpected</i> story. <br /><br /><i>“It’s got bad things in it. Bad words, bad people, bad scenes.”</i><br /><br />Hoover preempted <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11925514.Code_Name_Verity__Code_Name_Verity___1_" title="Code Name Verity (Code Name Verity, #1) by Elizabeth E. Wein" rel="nofollow noopener"> Verity</a>’s release with a warning of sorts—although facetious and comical in delivery, it’s something sensitive readers should take to heart. This storyline is <b>dark</b>, and the lives of the characters that inhabit the pages are far from perfect—so, don’t kid yourself into thinking this is something it’s <i>not</i>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11925514.Code_Name_Verity__Code_Name_Verity___1_" title="Code Name Verity (Code Name Verity, #1) by Elizabeth E. Wein" rel="nofollow noopener"> Verity</a> is horrifying, maddening, and what-the-hell-inducing, but it’s also sustenance for that bibliophile looking to satisfy a craving for something <i>different</i>. <br /><br />From chapter one, it’s blatantly obvious <i>this</i> comes from an entirely different side of Hoover’s psyche than her typical love stories. Blood spatter accompanies the all-consuming, addictive quality of her words. Storytelling with the power to crawl inside of your mind, take over, and demand your undivided attention. <br /><br />Lowen’s life is literally in shambles—her mom just passed, she’s broke, on the brink of eviction and even though she’s a talented author, the crippling anxiety involved with marketing herself to fans has made her work less than popular.<br /><br />It’s the opportunity of a lifetime that uproots Lowen from the hustle and bustle of Manhattan to the quiet Vermont countryside. Contracted by a publisher to ghostwrite the three remaining books in an uber-popular series after the author was involved in an accident, Lowen has a ton of work ahead. Research lands her in Verity Crawford’s home office, looking for anything that might indicate the direction the author wanted to take the series. Instead, she finds herself caught-up in Verity’s life. Living in her home, sleeping in her bed, and spending time with Verity's husband, Jeremy, and their young son. Inescapable is the grief and pain marring it all. <br /><br />Most surprising was the level of creepiness Hoover managed to incite. A level even some seasoned suspense writers fail to attain. From someone who reads in the genre consistently and watches horror, it’s quite the feat for me to feel this level of anxiety. For my stomach to be twisted in knots, in anticipation of what’s to come—but, it happened.<br /><br />And that finale . . . <i>stunning</i>. I was so sure I’d pinpointed exactly what was happening and <i>why</i>, but I was wrong. So very wrong. <br /><br />Hoover mentions in her <i>Acknowledgements</i> that this was an indie project she wanted to branch out and write on her own, which is commendable and exciting when you think about where her inner drive might take readers next. While there’s no denying her love stories are fierce, my hope is for <i>more</i> suspense. To be this taken with her first try, I can only imagine what that mind of hers might dream up next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14370197171707202463" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2655676498" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2655676498" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2655676498?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Emily May by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2655676498" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3072670111918984785"><blockquote><i>"Find what you love and let it kill you."</i><br/> -Charles Bukowski</blockquote><br/>Woah, this was <i>fuuuucked up</i>. It should really come with a warning: <b>do not start reading this at night if you want to sleep.</b><br/><br/>For two reasons, actually. One, it is so compulsively readable that it's almost impossible to put it down until you've finished it. And two, it is seriously creepy and disturbing. Warnings for depictions of child abuse and some graphic violence.<br/><br/>Perhaps this doesn't need to be said, but <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41957126.Verity' title='Verity by Colleen Hoover' rel='nofollow noopener'> Verity</a> is definitely not a reg</span>
  <span id="freeText3072670111918984785" style="display:none"><blockquote><i>"Find what you love and let it kill you."</i><br /> -Charles Bukowski</blockquote><br />Woah, this was <i>fuuuucked up</i>. It should really come with a warning: <b>do not start reading this at night if you want to sleep.</b><br /><br />For two reasons, actually. One, it is so compulsively readable that it's almost impossible to put it down until you've finished it. And two, it is seriously creepy and disturbing. Warnings for depictions of child abuse and some graphic violence.<br /><br />Perhaps this doesn't need to be said, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41957126.Verity" title="Verity by Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener"> Verity</a> is definitely not a regular Colleen Hoover romance. There's a love story, and sex, but it is predominantly a creepy thriller. And a mindfuck, if we're being honest. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41957126.Verity" title="Verity by Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener"> Verity</a> is mainly about three people - struggling author Lowen Ashleigh, a man called Jeremy Crawford, and Jeremy's wife, Verity, who was recently left incapacitated by a car accident. Verity is a successful writer, but she is no longer able to continue her bestselling series. That's why Lowen is brought in to complete the remaining three books. To do so, she stays at the couple's house so she can go through Verity's notes.<br /><br />But Lowen finds something else in Verity's office. An unfinished autobiography. As she reads, her fear grows. Lowen begins to dig into dark truths about the family and the deaths of their twin daughters. At the same time, she finds herself falling for Jeremy and wondering if perhaps she should reveal the truth to him.<br /><br />I don't want to say too much, <b>but I thought it was excellent</b>. Hoover expertly leads us on a winding trail of lies and manipulation. As the story is essentially Hoover - an author - writing about an author reading about another author, there's this constant sense that someone is lying to you-- but who is it? Now, that's not so easy to tell.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>I was good at spewing bullshit. It’s why I became a writer.</i>
</blockquote><br />This may seem like a bit of a backhanded compliment, but I think I enjoy Hoover’s fucked-up books so much because I usually find her regular romances kinda fucked up. <b>I like her books so much more when she's writing about trauma and morally-questionable characters</b> than when she's trying to sell me a douche as a love interest.<br /><br />It's a clever book, and I don't simply mean because of its twists and turns. It's clever because of the fear and uncertainty the author creates. That all three authors create. The aptly-named <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41957126.Verity" title="Verity by Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener"> Verity</a> is a novel about fictions and truths, about authors and characters, and about how it can sometimes be hard to separate the two.<br /><br />I found it absolutely riveting.<br /><br /><a href="http://emilymay.me" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3072670111918984785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2606426000" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2606426000" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2606426000?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2606426000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13715001390259283104">I've pulled up this review and tried to make the words come for a couple of days now, but every time I try to write the words all that comes to mind is <b>WTF Colleen</b>?! Obviously we were warned going in that this one would but much different than her other novels, but she didn't tell us that it would be so compulsive and I wouldn't be able to live my life while reading it. <i>How dare she??</i> But seriously, this book was so delicious in a seriously twisted way, and I feel slightly guilty admitting that </span>
  <span id="freeText13715001390259283104" style="display:none">I've pulled up this review and tried to make the words come for a couple of days now, but every time I try to write the words all that comes to mind is <b>WTF Colleen</b>?! Obviously we were warned going in that this one would but much different than her other novels, but she didn't tell us that it would be so compulsive and I wouldn't be able to live my life while reading it. <i>How dare she??</i> But seriously, this book was so delicious in a seriously twisted way, and I feel slightly guilty admitting that I loved <i>Verity</i> so much due to its dark and disturbing nature.<br /><br /><i>"Find what you love and let it kill you." -Charles Bukowski</i><br /><br />There's not really much you can say about the plot here, other than <s>read it for yourself ya filthy animal</s> you really should just go into it blind. Obviously there are numerous content warnings,<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[child abuse, murder, murder of a child, attempted home abortion, adultery, descriptive fatal pedestrian accident, etc.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> , but it you're open to picking up this book with as little knowledge of the story as possible it will be in your best interest. <br /><br /><i>"Most people come to New York to be discovered. The rest of us come here to hide."</i><br /><br />The characters here are deviously flawed, every last one of them, and I <b>love</b> this. I'm a sucker for storylines that feature the writing of a book inside the plot, and this was no exception. The varying between Low's present tense POV and the chapters featuring Verity's autobiography built the most exquisite tension, and by the end of the novel we are flipping pages as quickly as Low is, trying to decipher where this is going and what's going to happen. Also, that epilogue. That is all I will say, other than I'm respectful and grateful to CoHo for leaving this book without the neat wrapping and shiny bow. There are pieces of the story that are essentially left up to the reader to determine their thoughts on, and while a bloody and gruesome story, this will make a fabulous book club novel with copious discussion points. Highly recommended if you can stomach the content, but beware reader-once you pick it up, you certainly won't want to set it down until you turn the final page.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13715001390259283104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39749481-holly-b-semi-hiatus-until-jan?shelf=disturbing-content">disturbing-content</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2670185428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5585162939251792940">** UNPOPULAR OPINION<br/><br/>This is the second novel that I've read by the author.  I'm not really familiar with her writing or style, but I was seeing many 4-5 star ratings on this book and it was a "thriller" so that was enough to push me to give it a try. <br/><br/>There are many, many high reviews for the book so I'm not here to dissuade anyone from reading it. It just wasn't a good fit for me. I read hundreds of thriller/mysteries and love the genre.<br/><br/>I've read darker novels and enjoyed them, but this one gave</span>
  <span id="freeText5585162939251792940" style="display:none">** UNPOPULAR OPINION<br /><br />This is the second novel that I've read by the author.  I'm not really familiar with her writing or style, but I was seeing many 4-5 star ratings on this book and it was a "thriller" so that was enough to push me to give it a try. <br /><br />There are many, many high reviews for the book so I'm not here to dissuade anyone from reading it. It just wasn't a good fit for me. I read hundreds of thriller/mysteries and love the genre.<br /><br />I've read darker novels and enjoyed them, but this one gave me an uncomfortable feeling that it is hard to express. Was it because it involved the characters children? Maybe. Was it the graphic sex scenes? May have contributed  Was it the improbable plot? I don't usually have an issue with this if I'm entertained. I wasn't. I can't explain more without giving spoilers.<br /><br />Again, this novel didn't work for me. If you decide to read it, you may enjoy it like so many others. Just my opinion. I wish I could unread it.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2501669127" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2501669127" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2501669127?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2018-four-stars">2018-four-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2501669127" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8264559786340561406"><a href='https://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%2011/IMG_2615_zpsct96cwj1.png.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544459905i/26723344._SY540_.png' alt=' photo IMG_2615_zpsct96cwj1.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Have you ever finished a book and thought… WTF did I just read? <i>Verity</i> is one of those books that will do that to you. Word to the wise for CoHo fans: this is not your typical book from Colleen Hoover. It’s amazingly written and it’s a completely captivating read, but it’s so different from anything she’s ever put out before. <br/><i>
  <blockquote>“Some families are lucky enough to never experience a single tragedy. But then there are those families that seem to have tragedies waiting on the back burner. What </blockquote></i></span>
  <span id="freeText8264559786340561406" style="display:none"><a href="https://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%2011/IMG_2615_zpsct96cwj1.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544459905i/26723344._SY540_.png" alt=" photo IMG_2615_zpsct96cwj1.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Have you ever finished a book and thought… WTF did I just read? <i>Verity</i> is one of those books that will do that to you. Word to the wise for CoHo fans: this is not your typical book from Colleen Hoover. It’s amazingly written and it’s a completely captivating read, but it’s so different from anything she’s ever put out before. <br><i>
  <blockquote>“Some families are lucky enough to never experience a single tragedy. But then there are those families that seem to have tragedies waiting on the back burner. What can go wrong, goes wrong. And then gets worse.”</blockquote>
</i><br><i>Verity</i> is a complex story about an author who is ghost writing a series for Verity Crawford, an author who is injured in a way she can’t write right now- maybe ever. Her husband, Jeremy, commissions Lowen to do this work. Lowen goes to the Crawford’s house to do some research but that house and that family is more than she ever expected. While searching through old paperwork pertaining to the series Verity has written, she finds a manuscript of a truly messed up autobiography that changes her life and the life of the Crawford family forever. <br> <br>The word I would use to describe this book is <b>disturbing</b>. I was seriously disturbed the whole time I read. It wasn’t too spooky for me, but it was thrilling and horrifying at times. The writing was out of this world and the story messed with my mind. I’m not sure if I loved it, hated it, liked the characters or hated them. It’s a story that’s not always likable, but dang it was good. It was enthralling and made me think. That ending messed with my mind so bad, I don’t even know how to feel. <br><br>If you’re a fan of psychological thrillers with romance thrown in and don’t mind a book that’s disturbing and thrilling because it’s also brilliant, check out <i>Verity</i>. I’m glad I went outside the box with this one and read it!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8264559786340561406" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1574540863962795037">🎉 <b>FIVE MIND BLOWING STARS!</b>🎉<br/><br/>This one is a killer! So dark and disturbing. I was not expecting to love this one so much. Colleen Hoover writes romance books. This one is a thriller. I have seen authors go from romance to romantic suspense, but never have I seen an author go from Romance to a dark and disturbing crazy thriller. She knocked this one out of the ball park. <br/><br/>This one just blew my mind. I could not put this book down. I read it while fixing dinner and eating my dinner. I have never done </span>
  <span id="freeText1574540863962795037" style="display:none">🎉 <b>FIVE MIND BLOWING STARS!</b>🎉<br /><br />This one is a killer! So dark and disturbing. I was not expecting to love this one so much. Colleen Hoover writes romance books. This one is a thriller. I have seen authors go from romance to romantic suspense, but never have I seen an author go from Romance to a dark and disturbing crazy thriller. She knocked this one out of the ball park. <br /><br />This one just blew my mind. I could not put this book down. I read it while fixing dinner and eating my dinner. I have never done this before. There are so many jaw dropping moments. <br /><br />All of the characters were done so well. I could just vision them in my head. I love her writing style. This was one intense read. Let me tell you this author writes so well. OMG!OMG! OMG! The ending was just perfect. I loved that twist. Wow!<br /><br />I am not a romance fan but loved this thriller so much that I went to the library and did the unexpected. I got her book, Without Merit. Hoover just changed me into picking up a romance novel. That's how good her writing is. <br /><br />This book just tied with my favorite book for the year so far. When this writer writes another thriller, I will be snatching this one off the shelves right away. I strongly recommend this book to all thriller fans that love a disturbing and dark thriller. <br />I know! I know! I just get to overly excited when I love a book.<br /><br />I recommend this one to all thriller fans!!</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Cristina Zanfir  , Andreea Elena</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Dana by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1594906-kim">Kim</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21690081-dana-ilie?shelf=my-guilty-pleasure">my-guilty-pleasure</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2625114245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14174812854569818613">This book was disturbing in a way that is hard to put in words. Verity is pitched as a thriller and a romantic suspense book. Well, allow me to be as candid as I can: "Verity is a mind-fuck". Is Disturbing. Twisted. Creepy. It will have you questioning things. Brutal. Haunting.<br/>There is no question, the story is hypnotizing. ENGROSSING even if alarmingly disconcerting. And the cherry on top? The ending. That probably held the most savage plot twist I have encountered in a romantic book.<br/><br/>If this is</span>
  <span id="freeText14174812854569818613" style="display:none">This book was disturbing in a way that is hard to put in words. Verity is pitched as a thriller and a romantic suspense book. Well, allow me to be as candid as I can: "Verity is a mind-fuck". Is Disturbing. Twisted. Creepy. It will have you questioning things. Brutal. Haunting.<br />There is no question, the story is hypnotizing. ENGROSSING even if alarmingly disconcerting. And the cherry on top? The ending. That probably held the most savage plot twist I have encountered in a romantic book.<br /><br />If this is the niche that CoHo find and stick, baby I'm yours for life!<br /><br />Verity is not an easy read. I am not really even sure if I can say it was an enjoyable read. But it was brilliant. Amazingly well written and unputdownable, Colleen will leave you questioning everything.<br /><br />By the end of the book, I hate all characters....<br /><br />Thank you so much Kim for your indirect recommendation!</span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith">Meredith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2659300424" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1426369044876544239"><b>
  <i>4.5 stars<br/><br/>A manipulative mind f*ck that will keep you guessing!<br/><br/>Verity is a psychological thriller in which the lines between fiction and reality blur together creating an illusion of truth. </i>
</b><br/><br/>A struggling author is offered a lucrative deal: continue writing the popular a bestselling series, get out of debt and be in the presence of a sexy man. SOunds too good to be true? Lowen Ashleigh must find out for herself. She heads to Vermont and begins her journey into famous author Verity Crawford’s mi</span>
  <span id="freeText1426369044876544239" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>4.5 stars<br /><br />A manipulative mind f*ck that will keep you guessing!<br /><br />Verity is a psychological thriller in which the lines between fiction and reality blur together creating an illusion of truth. </i>
</b><br /><br />A struggling author is offered a lucrative deal: continue writing the popular a bestselling series, get out of debt and be in the presence of a sexy man. SOunds too good to be true? Lowen Ashleigh must find out for herself. She heads to Vermont and begins her journey into famous author Verity Crawford’s mind. While digging through Verity’s notes, she comes across a manuscript which appears to be Verity’s autobiography. Lowen gets caught up in Verity’s story that weaves together a tale of obsession, lies, and death. But one must wonder, is Lowen reading fact or fiction?<br /><br />This book sucked me in from the very beginning--it’s addictive and <b>VERY</b> hard to put down. <b>Verity’s chapters were truly batsh*t crazy.</b> Lowen’s narrative was quite interesting as well, but there were times when I was begging for her to pick up Verity’s manuscript again so that I could read another chapter of craziness. I had a theory early on and, while I was correct, I am still left wondering over the truth of Verity’s story. <b> <i>Verity</i> has all of the elements of a good thriller: It’s intense, dark, and very twisted. Best of all, it still has me questioning the different versions of the truth presented!<br /><br />Thank you to all of my Goodreads friends for putting this book on my radar! </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1426369044876544239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText11010506453938287669" style="display:none">want to know whats even more shocking than this dark and twisted book?? its the fact that one of the most suspenseful stories i have ever read is written by my fave <u>romance</u> author! like, how in the world does that happen!?! my mind is absolutely blown.<br /><br />im usually wary of when authors try to branch out beyond their known genre of writing. i respect it, but sometimes it doesnt work out for the best. luckily, CoHo totally smashed it with this! i am beyond shocked at how creepy and thrilling this story is. its as disturbing as everyone says it is. i honestly read it one sitting - its so compulsively easy to consume. and that ending! omg. i am reeling!<br /><br />i had no idea that CoHo, the queen of love, has such a sinister imagination, but i am here for it! i really hope she does more psychological thrillers in the future because my brain, my body, my soul is completely overwhelmed in the best way possible. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2622582182?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="user" itemprop="url" name="BernLuvsBooks " href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks">BernLuvsBooks </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=adult-reads">adult-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=fave-reads">fave-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2622582182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7768502548668002051"><b><i><u>Verity</u></i> left me completely speechless, unsettled and unabashedly begging CoHo to write more thrillers!!!</b><br/><br/>I found this story creepy, dark, addictive and absolutely unputdownable. Hoover has quite an imagination and as an avid thriller reader I was immediately drawn into the creepy world she created within the Crawford's home. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>"My mother used to say that houses have a soul, and if that's true, the soul of Verity Carwford's house is as dark as they come."</i>
</b><br/><br/>Lowen Ashleigh is a struggling writer with</span>
  <span id="freeText7768502548668002051" style="display:none"><b><i><u>Verity</u></i> left me completely speechless, unsettled and unabashedly begging CoHo to write more thrillers!!!</b><br /><br />I found this story creepy, dark, addictive and absolutely unputdownable. Hoover has quite an imagination and as an avid thriller reader I was immediately drawn into the creepy world she created within the Crawford's home. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"My mother used to say that houses have a soul, and if that's true, the soul of Verity Carwford's house is as dark as they come."</i>
</b><br /><br />Lowen Ashleigh is a struggling writer with no family and no place to call home. She is approached by bestselling author, Verity Crawford's husband to complete the last three books in a successful series his injured wife is unable to finish. Drawn to Jeremy Crawford and needing the financial stability this arrangement would provide Lowen agrees to complete the books and finds herself a guest in the Crawford home as she sorts through Verity's papers. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Some families are lucky enough to never experience a single tragedy. But then there are those families that see to have tragedies waiting on the back burner. What can go wrong, goes wrong. And then gets worse."</i>
</b><br /><br />The Crawford's have experienced devastating tragedy in the loss of their twin daughters. Lowen can't help but feel sympathy for the grieving Jeremy and his remaining son. Then she uncovers Verity's unfinished autobiography. Page upon page of bone-chilling, psychotic admissions. As Lowen uncovers Verity's deepest, darkest secrets things between her and Jeremy begin to intensify. <br /><br /><b>But is all as it seems within the Crawford house?</b><br /><br />There were many chilling &amp; disturbing moments here both in the present and via Verity's autobiography which we get to read select chapters of along with Lowen. I loved this foray into the romantic thriller world and certainly hope we will be seeing more of this from Hoover in the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7768502548668002051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2632119970" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8175750888549681782"><br/><b>C.R.A.Z.Y. To! The! Hilt!</b><br/><br/>CoHo has one vivid imagination, and I for one, am glad she shared this ‘way out there’ creative plot line with the rest of us.<br/><br/>Let me tell you there were so many “What the what?” moments, I had to keep reminding myself I wasn’t reading a Stephen King or Greer Hendricks novel. <br/><br/>I really wouldn’t put this in the romance category, albeit plenty of sex scenes are a plenty. It is totally more af a psychological thriller. <br/><br/>Now you might be saying to yourself, ‘But this is Colleen</span>
  <span id="freeText8175750888549681782" style="display:none"><br /><b>C.R.A.Z.Y. To! The! Hilt!</b><br /><br />CoHo has one vivid imagination, and I for one, am glad she shared this ‘way out there’ creative plot line with the rest of us.<br /><br />Let me tell you there were so many “What the what?” moments, I had to keep reminding myself I wasn’t reading a Stephen King or Greer Hendricks novel. <br /><br />I really wouldn’t put this in the romance category, albeit plenty of sex scenes are a plenty. It is totally more af a psychological thriller. <br /><br />Now you might be saying to yourself, ‘But this is Colleen Hoover and she writes romance novels.’ I know, right?!? Well, she ventured completely out of her box this go round!<br /><br />I think this would make a great buddy read. So much to digest, dissect and discuss. So ‘much’ still swirling in my head ;)<br /><br />I am really glad I refrained from reading anyone else’s review, despite the temptation. I know I continue to sound like a broken record in one review after the other, but good gracious sakes, go in blind, prepare to be gob-smacked and enjoy the outlandish ride!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3526420743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10302891252058630328">4.5 ⭐ for this book that is creepier than I expected! <br/><br/>A book within a book and, like Lowen, I couldn't stop reading 𝘚𝘰 𝘉𝘦 𝘐𝘵. Even though seeing the bits of dinner that sometimes gets stuck in my son's braces doesn't turn my stomach as much as parts of this story did 😉<br/><br/>Thank you Bren for your fantastic review that motivated me to read this!!</span>

<div id="review_2626536493" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2626536493" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2626536493?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=kindle-lending-library">kindle-lending-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=psychological-thriller">psychological-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2626536493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10557088189038275906">Verity by Colleen Hoover is a 2018 publication. <br/>Unlike so many rabid fans of this author, I have not read, to my knowledge, a single book by Colleen Hoover. (Although I did find one of her books languishing on my Kindle recently) <br/><br/>I see so many rave reviews for her novels, and some of them seem like books I would probably like, but for some reason I continue to associate her with YA books, which is not my favorite genre. But, when I saw this book on Kindle Unlimited and read the synopsis, I was i</span>
  <span id="freeText10557088189038275906" style="display:none">Verity by Colleen Hoover is a 2018 publication. <br />Unlike so many rabid fans of this author, I have not read, to my knowledge, a single book by Colleen Hoover. (Although I did find one of her books languishing on my Kindle recently) <br /><br />I see so many rave reviews for her novels, and some of them seem like books I would probably like, but for some reason I continue to associate her with YA books, which is not my favorite genre. But, when I saw this book on Kindle Unlimited and read the synopsis, I was instantly intrigued. If the book had been written by anyone else, I probably would have given it a pass, while congratulating myself on using my iron willpower to stick to my strict- no exceptions- psychological thriller diet. <br /><br />But, because I knew this book was a departure for this wildly popular writer, my curiosity won out. So much for my iron willpower...<br /><br />The setup is interesting-<br /><br /> Author, Lowen Ashleigh’s financial status is as dismal as her book sales. Her mother recently died after a lengthy illness and she’s fending off eviction notifications, when out of the blue she is given the incredible and lucrative opportunity of co- authoring a series with, or rather, for, the famous writer, Verity Crawford. Verity was in a horrible car crash and is no longer able to continue writing. Lowen doesn’t have to think too hard about accepting the job, especially when she sees the amount of money involved. <br /><br />Verity’s devoted husband, Jeremy, allows Lowen to live in their home while she goes through Verity’s notes on the series and acclimates herself with the tasks she’s been hired to perform. But when she stumbles across a Verity’s autobiography amongst her other work materials. Lowen rationalizes the need to read the manuscript, convincing herself it will help her better understand Verity. What she learns about the esteemed author will blow your mind!! <br /><br />Meanwhile, as Lowen immerses herself deeper and deeper into Verity’s memoir, a bond develops between Jeremy and Lowen. The attraction deepens as they spend more time together, until it becomes palpable and undeniable. However, Lowen has begun to irrationally fear Verity.<br /><br />Are her fears overwrought? Is her imagination playing tricks on her? <br /><br /> For long time fans of this author, this book could be a little like culture shock. But, for the seasoned readers of psychological thrillers, all this twisty darkness, and diabolical characterizations are par for the course. <br /><br />However, I must say that this one is more than just a departure for this author, it is a bit of a departure for the standard psychological thriller, as well. Many of you may not remember the surge in popularity of psychological thrillers back in the nineties, not just in books, but in movies, as well.<br /><br /> Back then, it was almost a requirement for a PT to be as sexually steamy, as it was edgy and suspenseful. I thought this book had that same feel, as it contained a lot more sexually explicit content than most standard PT’s written today. It should also be noted that many people have shelved this book in the romance category. However, in my opinion, this is not a romance, nor does it fall into the romantic suspense category, although there is a romantic element, if you wish to view it as such. It’s a pure psychological thriller, through and through. That’s just my take on it. <br /><br /><br />As far as PT’s go, this one is unique, very atmospheric and creepy, and even I, Miss jaded and burned out on PT’s, nearly jumped out of my skin on one occasion. The author thankfully keeps the story on an even keel, with no wild, unnecessary, or over the top twists. In fact, the twists are very well timed, and the suspense builds at a steady and effective pace. <br /><br /> Although the story is far from predictable, I did figure some things out in advance, and many seasoned PT readers will probably have a good inkling where everything is headed, as well. It’s an unavoidable ‘occupational hazard’ I think. Still, the final turn of the screw was very well done, and the book ended on a perfect note. I loved it! <br /><br />I am impressed by Ms. Hoover’s courage to step outside her comfort zone, taking a risk by writing outside of her usual genre. That she pulled this off, shouldn’t really be a surprise, though. Reading her bio, I see that she is a number one New York Times bestselling author. Ms. Hoover is a seasoned, professional writer and has been for some time. Let’s give her a little credit here. <br /><br />I hope her success with this book will widen her reading audience and I hope she will try her hand at this genre again someday. Meanwhile, I think it’s about time I checked out some of her romance and contemporary fiction novels.<br /><br />4 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="10557088189038275906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2626858258" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2626858258" />
    <a title="Misty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4348181-misty"><img alt="Misty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542045550p2/4348181.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2626858258?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Misty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Misty" href="/user/show/4348181-misty">Misty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4348181-misty?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2626858258&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2626858258" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10655496836865977846">Ok, this one has me scratching my head. I chose to read this piece of nonsense based on the myriad 5-star reviews on Amazon—I’m talking HUNDREDS. Now there are two reasons this novel may have so much positive feedback. First, it could be that there are hundreds of readers who don’t often step beyond this author’s normal genre (of which this book did not belong) and are simply ride-or-die fans. Second, it could be that I’ve gone round the twist and am missing the value. I’m betting on the former.</span>
  <span id="freeText10655496836865977846" style="display:none">Ok, this one has me scratching my head. I chose to read this piece of nonsense based on the myriad 5-star reviews on Amazon—I’m talking HUNDREDS. Now there are two reasons this novel may have so much positive feedback. First, it could be that there are hundreds of readers who don’t often step beyond this author’s normal genre (of which this book did not belong) and are simply ride-or-die fans. Second, it could be that I’ve gone round the twist and am missing the value. I’m betting on the former.<br /><br />The writing here is, admittedly, pretty amazing. Character development and plot movement, as well as the establishment of tone, is all done masterfully. What is ludicrous, however, is the plot itself. <br /><br />**SPOILER ALERT AHEAD** Verity is a well-known and well liked author with a huge fan base. She and her husband lose their young twin girls some months apart in separate tragedies, then Verity herself is in a car accident. The accident leaves her in a semi-vegetative state, unable to move or communicate. Her husband seeks to hire an author to finish the last three books his wife had promised as part of a series of nine. In steps Lowen, a talented author in her own right, though certainly not as famous as Verity. She travels to the couple’s home, where Verity is under constant care (fed, diapered, etc.), in order to look over the woman’s notes in preparation for the writing Lowen has been commissioned to complete. Whilst rummaging through Verity’s office, and falling in love with Verity’s husband, Lowen discovers a manuscript that is supposedly an autobiography written by Verity before her accident. It is beyond disturbing and paints the now comatose author as a raging psychopath who despised her twins, feeling only raging jealousy at the attention they garner from their father. So far so good, right? Here’s where it all goes to hell. VERITY IS FAKING HER INJURIES. Really? Doctors and nurses, specialists in their respective fields, can’t tell SHE IS FAKING IT?? For MONTHS? She has been cleaned, turned and fed and NO ONE KNEW? Additionally, we are to believe that she wrote the most disturbing things about herself and her children and labeled the manuscript an autobiography as a WRITING EXERCISE? What woman writes that she tried to abort her own children with a coat hanger as part of an exercise?? I could go on and on but I think you get the picture. Absurd is the only word that adequately conveys the entire premise. <br /><br />I wish someone, anyone, would have said to this author, “hey, you’re damn good, but this story just doesn’t make an iota of sense.” I’m left wishing back the hours it took me to read this insanely ridiculous drivel. Two stars for the obvious talent, but nless you are a die-hard fan of this writer, I’d skip this one altogether.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10655496836865977846" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2637465442?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susanne  Strong" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susanne  Strong" href="/user/show/4514828-susanne-strong">Susanne  Strong</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2637465442" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3340402419785701188"><b>3.85 Stars* (rounded up)<br/><br/>Well Darn It! This novel didn’t quite live up to the Hype. </b><br/><br/>“Verity” is a novel that I’ve seen crazy review after crazy review for and after a while, the hype got to both me and my book buddy, such that we decided to make it our New Year’s read. Admittedly, this book is, in fact, Whack (and entertaining at that) - however, I expected the ending to blow me away but after all the insane reviews I read, it was just kind of like “wah wah.” <br/><br/><b>“Verity” is my first novel by Colleen</b></span>
  <span id="freeText3340402419785701188" style="display:none"><b>3.85 Stars* (rounded up)<br /><br />Well Darn It! This novel didn’t quite live up to the Hype. </b><br /><br />“Verity” is a novel that I’ve seen crazy review after crazy review for and after a while, the hype got to both me and my book buddy, such that we decided to make it our New Year’s read. Admittedly, this book is, in fact, Whack (and entertaining at that) - however, I expected the ending to blow me away but after all the insane reviews I read, it was just kind of like “wah wah.” <br /><br /><b>“Verity” is my first novel by Colleen Hoover - it was eye-opening! Let’s chat about how salacious it is. Like wowza! </b> If that’s your thang, you’re definitely going to want to take a bite out of this one. It’s also a super fast read... Maybe it’s the salaciousness… but even I couldn’t tear my eyes away (true dat!, lol). <br /><br />When Lowen Ashleigh is hired to co-author the remaining books in a series for “Verity” Crawford who was in a debilitating accident, she has no idea what she has gotten herself into. Being offered a huge sum of money, she just can’t turn it down. Staying in Verity’s home with Jeremy, Verity’s husband and their son Crew so that she can pour through Verity’s library, Lowen discovers way more than she ever bargained for. <br /><br /><b>“Verity” is weird, wild and yes, quite wicked. It is also disturbing at times, I will not lie, that said, it is highly entertaining. </b> Had there not been so much hype built up around this novel, I think I would have enjoyed it more, such is life I suppose. I think most readers will LOVE this thus I think you should all dive in, the sooner, the better. <br /><br />Thank you so much to Kaceey for this book! Thank you also for reading this one with me - it was one wild ride! <br /><br />Published on Goodreads on 12.31.18.</span>

<div id="review_2544691301" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2544691301" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5032725-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525132364p2/5032725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2544691301?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/5032725-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2544691301" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3244947847127846913">Here's a book with some bite! It also gives new meaning to the term "if at first, you don't succeed, try, try again."<br/><br/>Colleen Hoover has created yet another highly readable, captivating, and fast read that is quite different from her other books.<br/><br/>Lowen Ashleigh is a struggling author who is dealing with the recent loss of her mother and the loss of a home when a writing job comes at just the right moment! Bestselling author, Verity Crawford, injured in an accident is not able to complete her succe</span>
  <span id="freeText3244947847127846913" style="display:none">Here's a book with some bite! It also gives new meaning to the term "if at first, you don't succeed, try, try again."<br /><br />Colleen Hoover has created yet another highly readable, captivating, and fast read that is quite different from her other books.<br /><br />Lowen Ashleigh is a struggling author who is dealing with the recent loss of her mother and the loss of a home when a writing job comes at just the right moment! Bestselling author, Verity Crawford, injured in an accident is not able to complete her successful series. Her husband, Jeremy Crawford has hired Lowen to complete his wife's series. Like Lowen, Jeremy is no stranger to loss. His twin daughters have both died tragically and his wife, Verity, has been in a terrible accident.<br /><br />When Lowen arrives at their home and begins to go through Verity's paperwork and notes, she discovers Verity's unfinished autobiography. Lowen can't stop reading, completely engrossed with Verity's admissions, secrets, and revelations. She wants to keep the journal a secret, but can she keep it to herself for long?<br /><br />There is a creepiness to this book as well as a sense of foreboding and dread. just as Lowen could not put down Verity's autobiography, I could not put this book down! Wanting to know what was going on, I dove into the pages and the lives of the characters. As the story progresses the suspense builds, I just knew something was going to happen! <br /><br />I go long stretches between reading Hoover's book and then wonder why as I have enjoyed all the ones I have read. As I mentioned, this is a little off the beaten path for her and this one also has more graphic sex scenes. Some won't mind, some will. But what will most think of the ending? <br /><br />Yes, that ending. I honestly did not see <b>THAT</b> coming. I thought she did a great job of pulling the wool over my eyes. Will the wool be pulled over yours as well? My only complaint - the ending felt abrupt. Interesting, yes.... but abrupt. Otherwise, this was quite the page-turner for me and I'm glad she tried something new. This one is darker, edgier, and more intense than her other books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3244947847127846913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2715463909" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2715463909" />
    <a title="Joey R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11232712-joey-r"><img alt="Joey R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528158785p2/11232712.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2715463909?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joey R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joey R." href="/user/show/11232712-joey-r">Joey R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2715463909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4826219503151820429">4.5 Stars —- I decided to read “Verity” by Colleen Hoover after seeing it had a full 5 star rating on Amazon with almost 2000 reviews. I never heard of Colleen Hoover, and when I discovered she primarily wrote romance novels, I almost didn’t read the book. After reading a plot summary and a few of the rave reviews I decided to give it a shot. After reading this book in less than 4 days, I can tell you Hoover is the real deal. The story is told from the perspective of Lowen, a struggling author, </span>
  <span id="freeText4826219503151820429" style="display:none">4.5 Stars —- I decided to read “Verity” by Colleen Hoover after seeing it had a full 5 star rating on Amazon with almost 2000 reviews. I never heard of Colleen Hoover, and when I discovered she primarily wrote romance novels, I almost didn’t read the book. After reading a plot summary and a few of the rave reviews I decided to give it a shot. After reading this book in less than 4 days, I can tell you Hoover is the real deal. The story is told from the perspective of Lowen, a struggling author, who is offered a lucrative job offer of finishing the final two books in a series by a very successful author who had been seriously injured in a car accident. She accepts the offer and goes to the home of Verity, the author who lives there in a vegetative state with her husband Jeremy. She agrees to stay for several days in order to go through all the notes and manuscripts of Verity that she keeps at the residence. This is where the book takes off as Lowen moves from investigating the prior works of Verity to investigating the lives of Verity and Jeremy. This author does a great job of building suspense and fear into an excellent plot. I couldn’t put it down. It definitely surpassed all expectations, and I hope Hoover decides to leave her days of romance novels behind her. The only criticism of the book is that you could tell Hoover enjoys writing about sex and for a thriller there is way too much detailed descriptions that were really unnecessary to the plot. But with that said I am a huge fan and will definitely be back if she writes another suspense novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4826219503151820429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2799858518" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
